Ruling on Finding the Hunted Animal Alive
States a concise ruling on hunted animal found alive

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a hunted animal is found alive and explain why slaughter is obligatory.

Core Idea
A hunted animal found alive must be slaughtered; otherwise, it is not halal.

In the Book of Hunting, the author of Al-Hidayah reminds us of a fundamental rule: if the hunter reaches the game animal while it is still alive, he must perform ritual slaughter (dhabh). This lesson recaps that concise ruling and its significance for halal meat.

Guided Path
1
Recall the scenario
The hunter shoots an animal (sayd) and later finds it alive, rather than dead from the shot.
The animal must be alive at the moment of reaching it.
2
State the ruling
The hunter must slaughter the animal (dhabh) immediately. In Hanafi terminology, this act is wajib (obligatory).
The Arabic phrase in the matn is 'ذكاه' (yudhakkihi).
3
Identify the consequence
If the hunter does not slaughter it, the meat remains haram (unlawful) — it is carrion (maytah).
Slaughter is a condition (shart) for halal meat.
4
Note the cross-reference
The author refers to a detailed discussion in the first chapter of the Book of Hunting, where all aspects and disagreements among schools are explained.
This passage is a memorization anchor; the details are elsewhere.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر شکار زندہ ہل جائے ذبح لازم ہے ورنہ حلال نہ ہو گا
كتاب الصيد
قال فان ادر که حيا ذكاه وقد بيناها بوجوهها والاختلاف فيها في الفصل الاول فلا نعيده.
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا پس اگر اس نے (رامی نے) شکار کو زندہ پالیا تو اس کو ذبح کرنے اور ہم اس مسئلہ کو مع اس کی تمام صورتوں کے اور اس میں اختلاف کو پہلی فصل میں بیان کر چکے ہیں پس ہم اس کا اعادہ نہیں کریں گے۔
تشریح اگر تیر پھینکنے والے کو شکار زند ہل جائے تو اب ذبح کرنا لازم ہے ورنہ حلال نہ ہوگا مصنف نے پہلی فصل میں ص ۴۸۰ ج ۴ پر اس مسئلہ کی تمام صورتیں اور اس میں اختلافات کو تفصیل سے بیان کر دیا ہے
He said: If he finds it alive, he should slaughter it. And we have already explained it with its aspects and the differences in the first chapter, so we will not repeat it.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn of Al-Hidayah, reminding the reader of the rule previously established: if a hunter wounds an animal and later finds it alive, he must slaughter it (dhabh) for it to be halal. The author refers to the detailed discussion in the first chapter, indicating that this is a settled ruling with no new elaboration here. The Urdu commentary emphasizes that slaughter is obligatory ('lazim') and without it the animal remains haram.

Key Terms
صید (sayd): The game animal that is hunted.
ذکاۃ (dhabh): Ritual slaughter of the animal.
رامی (rami): The person who shoots the arrow (the hunter).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a hunter do if he finds the game animal alive after shooting it?
A) He may eat it without further action.
B) He must slaughter it for it to be halal.
C) He must release it.
D) He must wait for it to die naturally.

Key Takeaway
A hunted animal found alive must be slaughtered by the hunter; otherwise, it remains haram.

Ruling When Hunted Animal Disappears and is Found Dead
Details the ruling and proofs for game that disappears after being hit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on game that disappears after being hit and explain why the continuation of pursuit determines its halal or haram status.

Core Idea
Persistent pursuit overrides the conjecture of other causes; abandonment makes the meat haram.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, the Hanafi school details a nuanced ruling regarding game that is hit by an arrow but disappears and is later found dead. The ruling hinges not on the time elapsed but on whether the hunter continued pursuing the animal. This lesson unpacks the textual proofs, the rational argument, and the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam Malik.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: (a) hunter continues pursuit and finds the animal dead — halal; (b) hunter abandons pursuit and later finds it dead — not halal. The ruling is conditional on the hunter's action.
The key variable is the hunter's persistence in seeking the animal.
2
Examine the first proof: the hadith
The Prophet's disapproval (karahah) of eating game that disappears is cited. The Hanafi school interprets this as an indication of prohibition (haram) when the hunter does not pursue, because the word 'لعل' (perhaps) indicates a strong possibility of another cause. But this prohibition is overridden when the hunter continues pursuit out of necessity.
The hadith is ahad, so it provides zanni proof.
3
Understand the rational proof (qiyas)
The passage argues that when a possibility of another cause of death exists (like vermin), the conjectural (mawhum) is treated as certain (muhaqqaq) in this context. Therefore, without overriding, the meat would be haram. However, necessity overrides because hunting cannot avoid such disappearances.
This is a form of istihsan.
4
Analyze the objection and answer
An objection is raised: why is conjecture overridden when the hunter pursues? The answer: because hunting cannot be free from animals disappearing; if we always declare such meat haram, hunting would become impractical. This is the principle of ضرورة (necessity). When the hunter gives up, there is no necessity, so the conjecture stands.
The objection arises from treating al-mawhum as al-muhaqqaq.
5
Compare with the Maliki position
Imam Malik distinguishes based on whether a night passes. The Hanafis argue that the hadith they narrate refutes Malik's view. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that a Hanafi may eat a game found after several days if he continued pursuit, while a Maliki may not if a night passed.
This shows how different usul principles lead to different rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شکار کو تیر لگا لیکن مشقت کر کے بھاگ گیا پھر مردہ ملا تو کیا حکم
قال واذا وقع السهم بالصيد فتحامل حتى غاب عنه ولم يزل في طلبه حتى اصابه ميتا اكل وان قعد عن طلبه ثم اصابه ميتا لم يوكل لماروى عن النبي عليه السلام انه كره اكل الصيد اذا غاب عن الرامي وقال لعل هوام الارض قتلته ولان احتمال الموت بسبب اخر قائم فما ينبغي ان يحل اكله لان الموهوم في هذا كالمتحقق لما روينا
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جب تیر شکار کو لگا ( جس سے وہ گرا) پھر مشقت کے ساتھ وہ بھا گا یہاں تک کہ شکاری سے غائب ہو گیا اور وہ برابر اس کی تلاش میں رہا یہاں تک کہ اس نے اسکو مردہ پایا تو وہ کھایا جائے گا اور اگر وہ اس کی طلب سے بیٹھ رہا پھر اس کو مرا ہوا پایا تو نہیں کھایا جائے گا بوجہ اس کے کہ نبی علیہ السلام سے مروی ہے کہ آپ نے شکار کھانے کو مکروہ جانا جبکہ وہ رامی سے غائب ہو جائے اور فرمایا شاید کہ زمین کے جانوروں نے اس کو مار ڈالا ہو اور اسلئے کہ دوسرے سبب سے موت کا احتمال قائم ہے پس یہ بات مناسب نہیں کہ اس کا کھانا حلال ہو اس لئے کہ موہوم اس باب میں تحقیق کے مثل ہے اس روایت کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم روایت کر چکے ہیں ۔ تشریح شکار کو تیرلگا اور وہ گرا لیکن وہ مشقت برداشت کر کے بھاگا اور غائب ہو گیا پھر وہ مالیکن مرا ہوا ملا تو اب کیا حکم ہے؟ تو دیکھا کہ تیر مارنے والا برابر اس کی تلاش میں ہے یا بیٹھ رہا پہلی صورت میں حلال ہے اور دوسری میں حرام ہے جس کی مصنف نے دو دلیلیں ذکر کی ہیں۔
ا۔ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس کے کھانے کو نا پسند فرماتے ہوئے فرمایا شاید کہ حشرات الارض نے اس کو مار دیا ہو۔ -۲- دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ احتمال ہے کہ یہ شکار آپ کے تیر کے علاوہ کسی اور سبب سے مر گیا ہو تو پھر اس کا کھانا مناسب نہیں ہے۔
سوال ... آپ نے امر موہوم پر بنیاد کیسے رکھی جبکہ اس کے مقابلہ میں امر تحقق موجود ہے یعنی تیر مارتا جواب ... شکار کے باب میں موہوم متحقیق کے درجہ میں ہے اور جب دونوں مساوی ہو گئے تو تعارض ہوگیا اور بر وقت تعارض حرمت کو ترجیح دی گئی ہے ( کما ہو الاصل)
الا انا اسقطنا اعتباره مادام فى طلبه ضرورة ان لا يعرى الاصطياد عنه ولا ضرورة فيما اذا قعد عن طلبه لامكان التحرز عن توار يكون بسبب عمله والذى رويناه حجة على مالك في قوله ان ماتوارى عنه اذا لم بيت يحل فاذا بات ليلة لا يحل
ترجمہ اگر ہم نے ساقط کر دیا موہوم کے اعتبار کرنے کو جب تک کہ وہ اس کی طلب میں ہو اس بات کی ضرورت کی وجہ سے شکار کرنا اس سے خالی نہیں ہوتا اور کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے اس صورت میں جبکہ وہ اس کی طلب سے بیٹھ رہے بچاؤ کے ممکن ہونے کی وجہ سے ایسے چھپنے سے جو صائد فصل کی جہت سے ہو اور وہ حدیث جس کو ہم نے روایت کیا ہے مالک پر حجت ہے ان کے یہ کہنے میں کہ وہ شکار جو اسے چھپا ہے جبکہ رات نہ گذرے تو حلال اور اگر رات گذر جائے تو حلال نہیں ہے۔ تشریح یہاں ایک اعتراض وارد ہوتا ہے کہ جب موہوم تحقیق کے مثل ہے تو شکاری اگر چہ شکار کی تلاش میں ہے اور پھر اس کو مردہ پایا ہے تو اب بھی اس میں احتمال ہے کہ اس کو ہوام الارض نے مارڈالا ہو اور موہوم تحقیق کے مثل ہوتا ہے لہذا آپ کو چاہینے کی آپ اس کو بھی تو حرام قرار دیں حالانکہ آپ اس کو حلال کہتے ہیں۔ جواب مصنف نے الانا استقطنا .. المہ سے اس اعتراض کا جواب دیا ہے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ شکار کرنا عموماً اس سے خالی نہیں ہوتا کہ شکار چھپ جاتا ہے اور غائب ہو جاتا ہے اور اگر چھپتے ہی حرمت کا حکم جاری کر دیا جائے تو اصطیاد کا دروازہ بند کرنا لازم آئے گا۔
اور رہی دوسری صورت جبکہ شکاری شکار کی طلب سے بیٹھ رہے کہ اس سے احترازممکن ہے کہ وہ نہ بیٹے اور برابر شکار کا پیچھا کرتار ہے تو گویا یہاں غائب ہونا ایسے فعل کی وجہ سے ہے جو شکاری کا فعل ہے یعنی اس کا بیٹھ رہنا مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم نے جو حدیث بیان کی ب لعل هو ام الارض قتلته یہ حدیث امام مالک کے خلاف حجت ہے کیونکہ انہوں نے ایسے شکار کے بارے میں یہ فرمایا ہے کہ اگر اس پر رات گذرگئی تو کھانا حلال نہیں ہے اور اگر رات نہیں گذری تو حلال ہے۔ تنبیہ حدیث صحیح ہے اذا رمیست سهمک فغاب ثلاثة ايام و ادر کته فكله مالم ينتن (رواه مسلم واحمد و ابوداؤد) لہذا امام مالک پر حجت ہونے کی بات غیر مناسب ہے لہذا یہاں یہ تاویل کی جائے گی کہ اس حدیث کا عمل یہ ہے کہ وہ طلب سے بیٹھا نہ ہو بلکہ برابر طلب کرتا رہے اور جس حدیث کو صاحب ہدایہ نے ذکر کیا ہے اس کو اس حالت پر محمول کیا جائے جبکہ وہ طلب سے بیٹھ رہے وفیہ تفصيل مذكور في الشامي ص ۳۰۲ ج ۵
He said: And if the arrow hits the game and it struggles until it disappears from him, and he does not cease pursuing it until he finds it dead, he may eat it. But if he gives up pursuit and then finds it dead, he may not eat it, because it is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he disapproved of eating game when it disappears from the shooter and said: 'Perhaps the vermin of the earth have killed it.' And because the possibility of death from another cause exists, so it is not proper to consider its eating permissible, because the conjectural in this case is like the certain, due to the hadith we have narrated.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling from Al-Hidayah on the permissibility of game that is hit by an arrow but then disappears and is found dead. The matn states two scenarios: (1) If the hunter continues pursuing the animal until he finds it dead, it is halal. (2) If he abandons the pursuit and later finds it dead, it is not halal. Two proofs are given: a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) indicating disapproval of eating game that disappears from the shooter, implying that the possibility of another cause of death (vermin) is considered; and a rational argument that when there is a possibility of death from another cause, it is not permissible to eat. An objection is raised: how can conjecture (al-mawhum) be given weight over certainty (al-muhaqqaq) that the arrow hit? The answer is that in hunting, conjecture is treated as certain because disappearance is common, but this is only overridden when the hunter continues pursuit out of necessity (since hunting cannot be free from such disappearances). When the hunter gives up, the conjecture is not overridden because he can avoid it by continuing pursuit. The passage then addresses Imam Malik's view, which distinguishes based on whether a night passed; the Hanafis argue that the hadith they narrated is evidence against Malik, and the correct criterion is the persistence of pursuit, not the passing of time. A supplementary note mentions a different hadith (Muslim, Ahmad, Abu Dawud) that is also considered, but the author explains that it applies when the hunter does not sit back, reconciling the texts.

Key Terms
صید (sayd): The game animal that is hunted.
رامی (rami): The shooter (hunter).
موہوم (mawhum): That which is conjectural or probable, not certain.
متحقق (muhaqqaq): That which is certain or established.
طلب (talab): Pursuit of the game by the hunter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, which of the following is required for game that disappears after being hit to be halal?
A) The hunter must find it within one night.
B) The hunter must have continued pursuing it.
C) The animal must die immediately.
D) The arrow must remain in the animal.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of game that disappears after being shot depends on whether the hunter continued pursuing it, not on the time elapsed.

Game with an Extraneous Wound Is Not Halal
Supplementary ruling on extraneous wounds in hunting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on game found with an additional wound and apply the condition that the animal must be killed solely by the hunter's weapon.

Core Idea
An extraneous wound makes the meat haram because the cause of death is uncertain and avoidable.

This lesson examines a supplementary ruling in hunting: if the hunter finds the game with a wound that was not caused by his own arrow (or dog), the meat is not permissible. The key principle is that the hunter must ensure that the animal was killed solely by his lawful means; any other wound introduces an avoidable conjecture about the cause of death. We will also see that the same logic applies when using a hunting dog.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central act and its baseline ruling
The act is hunting game with a weapon (arrow) or a trained dog. The baseline ruling is that if the animal is killed by the hunter's lawful means, it is halal.
2
Recognize the critical condition
The condition for halal is that no non-hunter-caused wound exists on the animal. If such a wound is found, the meat is not halal.
The text says 'لا يحل' (it is not halal).
3
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
The presence of an extraneous wound creates a conjecture (wahm) that the animal may have died from that wound. Since the hunter could have avoided causing that wound (by being more careful or not hunting in that area), this conjecture is considered effective and renders the meat haram.
This is unlike the conjecture from vermin (hawam al-ard) which is unavoidable.
4
Extend the ruling to hunting with a dog
The same rule applies if the dog causes an additional wound beyond the hunter's control. The analogy (qiyas) is explicit in the text.
The text says: 'والجواب في ارسال الكلب في هذا كالجواب في الرمي'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو وجد به جراحة سوى جراحة سهمه لا يحل لانه موهوم يمكن الاحتراز عنه فاعتبر محرما بخلاف وهم الهوام والجواب في ارسال الكلب فى هذا كالجواب في الرمي في جميع ما ذكرناه
And if he finds on it a wound other than his arrow's wound, it is not halal, because it is conjectural and can be avoided, so it is considered haram, unlike the conjecture of vermin. And the answer regarding sending the dog in this is like the answer regarding shooting in all that we have mentioned.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This is a supplementary ruling from the matn: if the hunter finds the game with a wound that was not caused by his own arrow, the meat is not halal. The reasoning is that the possibility that the animal died from that other wound is a conjecture (mawhum) that can be avoided—unlike the conjecture of vermin (hawam al-ard) which is beyond the hunter's control. Since the hunter could have avoided causing that additional wound, the conjecture is effective and renders the meat haram. The same principle applies when hunting with a dog: if the dog causes an additional wound, the rule is analogous to the case of shooting. The reference to 'all that we have mentioned' points back to the earlier discussion about pursuit and conjecture.

Key Terms
جراحة (jarahah): A wound or injury on the game animal.
سهم (sahm): Arrow (the hunter's weapon).
ارسال الكلب (irsal al-kalb): Sending a dog to hunt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a hunter finds that the hunted animal has a wound that was not caused by his arrow?
A) It is halal because the arrow hit it.
B) It is not halal because the cause of death is uncertain.
C) It is makruh but still permissible.
D) It is halal only if the arrow wound is deeper.

Key Takeaway
An extraneous wound on game, even if the hunter's arrow also struck, makes the meat haram because the cause of death is uncertain and avoidable.

Ruling on Game with Additional Wounds
Explains the ruling for game with wounds not from the hunter's weapon

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for game found dead with additional wounds and explain the distinction between avoidable and unavoidable doubt.

Core Idea
Game with an additional wound is haram if the doubt is avoidable; unavoidable doubts are disregarded.

In the Hanafi school, hunting is governed by principles that balance the hunter's intention with the reality of the wild. One key issue is when the hunter finds his game dead but notices wounds not caused by his own arrow or dog. This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies when such doubt renders the game unlawful. The ruling hinges on whether the doubt could have been avoided by the hunter's diligence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is finding game dead with a wound besides the hunter's arrow. The ruling in the text is that it is not halal (haram).
This applies whether the hunter used a bow or a trained dog.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof istihsan: the principle that avoidable doubt (wahm) in hunting is treated as certainty, making the game prohibited.
Contrast with unavoidable doubt from insects (hawam) which is disregarded.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The additional wound creates a doubt that the death might have been caused by it. Since the hunter can avoid this by retrieving quickly or checking, the doubt is considered prohibitive.
The doubt is no longer unavoidable once the hunter has the opportunity to inspect the game.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Malik holds a different view on game that disappears overnight: he said halal if no night passes, haram if it does. The Hanafi school disagrees, tying the ruling to whether the hunter sat down from pursuit.
The hadith used by Malik is interpreted in the Hanafi school to apply only when the hunter continues pursuit.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi and is supported by the authentic hadith and the principle of avoiding hardship in hunting.
The authority is Zahir al-Riwayah, and no intra-Hanafi dispute exists on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الا انا اسقطنا اعتباره مادام فى طلبه ضرورة ان لا يعرى الاصطياد عنه ولا ضرورة فيما اذا قعد عن طلبه لامكان التحرز عن توار يكون بسبب عمله والذى رويناه حجة على مالك في قوله ان ماتوارى عنه اذا لم بيت يحل فاذا بات ليلة لا يحل ترجمہ اگر ہم نے ساقط کر دیا موہوم کے اعتبار کرنے کو جب تک کہ وہ اس کی طلب میں ہو اس بات کی ضرورت کی وجہ سے شکار کرنا اس سے خالی نہیں ہوتا اور کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے اس صورت میں جبکہ وہ اس کی طلب سے بیٹھ رہے بچاؤ کے ممکن ہونے کی وجہ سے ایسے چھپنے سے جو صائد فصل کی جہت سے ہو اور وہ حدیث جس کو ہم نے روایت کیا ہے مالک پر حجت ہے ان کے یہ کہنے میں کہ وہ شکار جو اسے چھپا ہے جبکہ رات نہ گذرے تو حلال اور اگر رات گذر جائے تو حلال نہیں ہے۔ تشریح یہاں ایک اعتراض وارد ہوتا ہے کہ جب موہوم تحقیق کے مثل ہے تو شکاری اگر چہ شکار کی تلاش میں ہے اور پھر اس کو مردہ پایا ہے تو اب بھی اس میں احتمال ہے کہ اس کو ہوام الارض نے مارڈالا ہو اور موہوم تحقیق کے مثل ہوتا ہے لہذا آپ کو چاہینے کی آپ اس کو بھی تو حرام قرار دیں حالانکہ آپ اس کو حلال کہتے ہیں۔ جواب مصنف نے الانا استقطنا .. المہ سے اس اعتراض کا جواب دیا ہے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ شکار کرنا عموماً اس سے خالی نہیں ہوتا کہ شکار چھپ جاتا ہے اور غائب ہو جاتا ہے اور اگر چھپتے ہی حرمت کا حکم جاری کر دیا جائے تو اصطیاد کا دروازہ بند کرنا لازم آئے گا۔ اور رہی دوسری صورت جبکہ شکاری شکار کی طلب سے بیٹھ رہے کہ اس سے احترازممکن ہے کہ وہ نہ بیٹے اور برابر شکار کا پیچھا کرتار ہے تو گویا یہاں غائب ہونا ایسے فعل کی وجہ سے ہے جو شکاری کا فعل ہے یعنی اس کا بیٹھ رہنا مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم نے جو حدیث بیان کی ب لعل هو ام الارض قتلته یہ حدیث امام مالک کے خلاف حجت ہے کیونکہ انہوں نے ایسے شکار کے بارے میں یہ فرمایا ہے کہ اگر اس پر رات گذرگئی تو کھانا حلال نہیں ہے اور اگر رات نہیں گذری تو حلال ہے۔ تنبیہ حدیث صحیح ہے اذا رمیست سهمک فغاب ثلاثة ايام و ادر کته فكله مالم ينتن (رواه مسلم واحمد و ابوداؤد) لہذا امام مالک پر حجت ہونے کی بات غیر مناسب ہے لہذا یہاں یہ تاویل کی جائے گی کہ اس حدیث کا عمل یہ ہے کہ وہ طلب سے بیٹھا نہ ہو بلکہ برابر طلب کرتا رہے اور جس حدیث کو صاحب ہدایہ نے ذکر کیا ہے اس کو اس حالت پر محمول کیا جائے جبکہ وہ طلب سے بیٹھ رہے وفیہ تفصيل مذكور في الشامي ص ۳۰۲ ج ۵۔ شکار میں تیر کے علاوہ کوئی زخم ہو تو شکار حلال نہیں۔ ولو وجد به جراحة سوى جراحة سهمه لا يحل لانه موهوم يمكن الاحتراز عنه فاعتبر محرما بخلاف وهم الهوام والجواب في ارسال الكلب فى هذا كالجواب في الرمي في جميع ما ذكرناه ترجمہ اور اگر شکار میں کوئی زخم اپنے تیر کے زخم کے علاوہ پایا تو وہ حلال نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ یہ ایسا موہوم جس سے احتراز ممکن ہے اور اس کو محرم شمار کیا جائے گا بخلاف ہوام کے اور جواب کتے کے چھوڑنے میں اس سلسلہ میں رمی کے جواب کے مثل ہے ان تمام صورتوں میں جن کو ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے۔ تشریح جب شکاری نے شکار کو پایا اور وہ مرا ہوا ہے تو اسکا تفصیلی حکم گذر چکا ہے لیکن یہ حکم اس وقت ہے کہ اس کے تیر کے علاوہ کا زخم شکار میں نہ ہو اور اگر اس کے علاوہ کوئی اور زخم ملے تو اب وہ حرام ہے خواہ وہ برابر تلاش کرتا رہے یا بیٹھ رہا ہو کیونکہ ہمیشہ ایسا نہیں ہوتا کہ اس کے زخم کے علاوہ کوئی اور زخم شکر کو لگے تو یہ ایسا امر موہوم ہے جس سے بچاؤ ممکن ہے اور باب صید میں موہوم مثل محقق کے ہوتا ہے اور بچاؤ بھی ممکن ہے تو یہاں موہوم کو محرم قرار دیا جائے گا جیسے محقق محرم ہوتا ہے۔ رہا مسئلہ ہوام کے وہم کا تو اس سے احتراز غیر ممکن ہے کیونکہ شکار زمین پر تو ضرور گرے گا اور زمین ہوام سے خالی نہیں رہتی تو جب تک وہ بیٹھ نہ رہے اس موہوم کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا اور شکار کو حلال قرار دیا جائے گا پھر کسی نے تیر پھینکا ہو یا کتا چھوڑا ہو تمام مذکورہ صورتوں میں حکم برابر ہے یعنی کتا چھوڑا اور کتے نے اس کو زخمی کر دیا اب وہ بھاگا پھر مرا ہوا ملا تو اب بھی وہی حکم ہے کہ اگر بیٹھ رہا تھا تو حرام ورنہ حلال ہے اور اگر کتے کے زخم کے علاوہ اور زخم اس میں ہے تو پھر دونوں صورتوں میں حلال نہ ہو گا۔
Except that we disregard the doubt as long as he is in pursuit, because hunting cannot be free from it, and there is no necessity when he sits down from pursuit because avoidance is possible for a concealment that occurs due to his action. And the hadith we narrated is a proof against Malik in his saying: that the game that disappears, if it does not spend a night, is halal, but if it spends a night, it is not halal. Translation: If we have disregarded the consideration of the doubt as long as he is in pursuit, due to the necessity that hunting is not free from it, and there is no necessity in the case when he sits down from pursuit, because avoidance is possible for such concealment that is due to his action. And the hadith we narrated is a proof against Malik in his saying that the game that disappears, if it does not spend a night, is halal, and if it spends a night, it is not halal. Commentary: Here an objection arises: when the doubt is like certainty, then the hunter, even if he is searching for the game and then finds it dead, there is still a possibility that the insects of the earth killed it, and the doubt is like certainty; therefore you should declare it also haram, whereas you say it is halal. The author answered this objection with 'except that we disregard...' The gist of the answer is that hunting is generally not free from the game hiding and disappearing; if you apply the ruling of prohibition as soon as it hides, then the door of hunting would be closed. As for the second case when the hunter sits down from pursuit, avoidance is possible by not sitting and continuing to pursue; so here the disappearance is due to the hunter's own action. The author says that the hadith we narrated is a proof against Malik, because they said about such game that if a night passes, it is not halal, and if not, it is halal. Note: The authentic hadith 'When you shoot your arrow and it disappears for three days and you find it, eat it as long as it has not become putrid' - so the statement that it is a proof against Malik is inappropriate; therefore it will be interpreted that the hadith applies when he is not sitting down from the pursuit but continues pursuing. And the hadith mentioned by the author of al-Hidayah is applied to the state when he is sitting down from pursuit. Details are in al-Shami vol.5 p.302. If the game has a wound besides the wound of his arrow, it is not halal, because it is a doubt that can be avoided, so it is considered a prohibition, unlike the doubt of insects. And the answer concerning releasing the dog is like the answer concerning shooting in all that we have mentioned. Translation: And if the game has any wound besides the wound of his arrow, it will not be halal, because it is a doubt from which avoidance is possible, and it will be considered a prohibition, unlike the doubt of insects. And the answer concerning releasing the dog is like the answer concerning shooting in all the cases we have mentioned. Commentary: When the hunter finds the game and it is dead, its detailed ruling has passed. But this ruling is when there is no wound besides his arrow. If there is any other wound, then it is haram, whether he continued searching or sat down, because it is not always that another wound besides his happens; this is a matter of doubt from which avoidance is possible, and in the chapter of hunting, doubt is treated like certainty, and since avoidance is possible, here the doubt will be considered a prohibition just as certainty is prohibited. As for the matter of the doubt of insects, avoidance is impossible because the game will necessarily fall on the ground, and the ground is not free of insects. So until he sits down, this doubt is not considered, and the game is declared halal. Then whether one shoots an arrow or releases a dog, the ruling is the same in all mentioned cases: if the dog released and it wounded the game, then it ran and was found dead, the same ruling applies: if he sat down, it is haram, otherwise halal. And if there is a wound besides the dog's wound, then in both cases it will not be halal.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning game found dead with wounds. It begins by addressing an objection: if doubt is treated like certainty, why is game found dead after being shot not automatically haram? The author explains that hunting necessarily involves the game disappearing; if every doubt made it haram, hunting would be impossible. However, if the hunter sits down and stops pursuing, then the doubt is avoidable, so the game becomes haram if found dead. The hadith narrated (about the arrow and three days) is used as a proof against Imam Malik's position that the game is halal if the night has not passed. The commentator notes that the authentic hadith is actually more general, so it is interpreted to apply when the hunter continues pursuit. Then a new ruling is introduced: if the game has a wound besides the hunter's arrow, it is not halal, because this doubt can be avoided by checking the game. This is contrasted with the doubt of insects (hawam), which is unavoidable because the game falls on the ground. The same ruling applies whether the hunter uses an arrow or a dog. The key principle is that avoidable doubts (wahm) are considered prohibitive in the chapter of hunting, whereas unavoidable doubts are disregarded.

Key Terms
موهوم (mawhum): A doubt or uncertainty that can be avoided by the hunter.
هوام (hawām): Insects or vermin that might kill the game on the ground.
صائد (ṣā'id): The hunter.
رمي (ramy): Shooting an arrow or bullet at game.
ارسال الكلب (irsāl al-kalb): Releasing a trained hunting dog.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a hunter finds a game animal dead with a wound from his arrow and also a wound from a predator that could have been avoided, what is the ruling?
A) It is halal because the hunter's arrow caused the death.
B) It is haram because the additional wound creates an avoidable doubt.
C) It is halal because the hunter was pursuing it continuously.
D) It is makruh because of the doubt.

Key Takeaway
Game with an additional avoidable wound is haram; for disappearance, the ruling depends on whether the hunter continued pursuit or sat down.

Additional Wound on Hunted Animal: When It Becomes Haram
Ruling on hunted animal with additional wound

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a hunted animal with an additional wound and distinguish the exception for insects (hawam) on the basis of avoidance.

Core Idea
An additional wound on a hunted animal makes it haram because the uncertainty is avoidable, except when caused by insects (hawam) as they are unavoidable.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on a hunted animal that has another wound besides the hunter's arrow or dog. The text from Al-Hidayah explains that such an animal is haram due to the principle that mawhum (uncertainty) is treated like certainty when avoidance is possible. However, an important exception is made for insects (hawam), which are disregarded because the hunter cannot avoid them. Understanding this principle is key to correctly determining the permissibility of hunted game.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A hunter finds a dead animal with his own wound plus another wound from an unknown source.
The additional wound could be from another animal, a rock, or a person.
2
Apply the principle of mawhum
In hunting, mawhum (uncertainty) is treated like muhqaq (certainty) if avoidance is possible. Since the hunter could have avoided the additional wound (e.g., by waiting or retrieving the animal immediately), the animal is haram.
This is a key Hanafi rule in the chapter of hunting.
3
Recognize the exception for insects
If the additional wound is from insects (hawam), avoidance is impossible because the animal must fall to the ground, which is never free of insects. Therefore, the animal remains halal.
The hunter cannot prevent insects from landing on the dead animal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ اور اگر شکار میں کوئی زخم اپنے تیر کے زخم کے علاوہ پایا تو وہ حلال نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ یہ ایسا موہوم جس سے احتراز ممکن ہے اور اس کو محرم شمار کیا جائے گا بخلاف ہوام کے اور جواب کتے کے چھوڑنے میں اس سلسلہ میں رمی کے جواب کے مثل ہے ان تمام صورتوں میں جن کو ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے۔ تشریح جب شکاری نے شکار کو پایا اور وہ مرا ہوا ہے تو اسکا تفصیلی حکم گذر چکا ہے لیکن یہ حکم اس وقت ہے کہ اس کے تیر کے علاوہ کا زخم شکار میں نہ ہو اور اگر اس کے علاوہ کوئی اور زخم ملے تو اب وہ حرام ہے خواہ وہ برابر تلاش کرتا رہے یا بیٹھ رہا ہو کیونکہ ہمیشہ ایسا نہیں ہوتا کہ اس کے زخم کے علاوہ کوئی اور زخم شکر کو لگے تو یہ ایسا امر موہوم ہے جس سے بچاؤ ممکن ہے اور باب صید میں موہوم مثل محقق کے ہوتا ہے اور بچاؤ بھی ممکن ہے تو یہاں موہوم کو محرم قرار دیا جائے گا جیسے محقق محرم ہوتا ہے۔ رہا مسئلہ ہوام کے وہم کا تو اس سے احتراز غیر ممکن ہے کیونکہ شکار زمین پر تو ضرور گرے گا اور زمین ہوام سے خالی نہیں رہتی تو جب تک وہ بیٹھ نہ رہے اس موہوم کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا اور شکار کو حلال قرار دیا جائے گا پھر کسی نے تیر پھینکا ہو یا کتا چھوڑا ہو تمام مذکورہ صورتوں میں حکم برابر ہے یعنی کتا چھوڑا اور کتے نے اس کو زخمی کر دیا اب وہ بھاگا پھر مرا ہوا ملا تو اب بھی وہی حکم ہے کہ اگر بیٹھ رہا تھا تو حرام ورنہ حلال ہے اور اگر کتے کے زخم کے علاوہ اور زخم اس میں ہے تو پھر دونوں صورتوں میں حلال نہ ہو گا۔
Translation: And if in the hunted animal any wound is found other than the wound of his own arrow, then it will not be permissible (halal), because this is a matter of uncertainty (mawhum) from which avoidance is possible, and it will be considered prohibited (muharram), unlike the case of insects (hawam). And the answer regarding letting the dog go in this context is like the answer regarding shooting in all these cases that we have mentioned. Commentary: When the hunter finds the hunted animal and it is dead, its detailed ruling has already passed. But this ruling is when there is no wound on the animal other than his arrow. If besides that another wound is found, then it is forbidden (haram), whether he kept searching or sat down, because it is not always the case that no other wound besides his wound appears on the hunted animal. So this is a matter of uncertainty (mawhum) from which avoidance is possible. And in the chapter of hunting, mawhum is like muhqaq (certain). And since avoidance is possible, here the mawhum will be considered prohibited, just as muhqaq is prohibited. As for the issue of the uncertainty from insects (hawam), avoidance from that is impossible because the hunted animal must fall to the ground, and the ground is not free of insects. So unless he sits down (to watch), that mawhum will not be considered and the hunted animal will be declared halal. Then whether someone shot an arrow or let a dog go, the ruling is the same in all mentioned cases; that is, if he let the dog go and the dog wounded it, then it ran away and then was found dead, then the same ruling applies: if he sat down, it is haram; otherwise halal. And if there is another wound besides the dog's wound, then in both cases it will not be halal.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hidayah regarding a hunted animal that has an additional wound besides the hunter's own arrow or dog's bite. The author explains that if such an additional wound is found, the animal is haram because this is a case of mawhum (uncertainty) that can be avoided by the hunter. In the chapter of hunting, the principle is that mawhum is treated like muhqaq (certain) when avoidance is possible. The hunter could have waited or ensured no other wound was inflicted. Therefore, the animal is prohibited. An exception is made for hawam (insects) because it is impossible to prevent insects from landing on the animal after it falls to the ground; since avoidance is impossible, that uncertainty is disregarded and the animal is halal. The same ruling applies to both shooting with an arrow and hunting with a dog.

Key Terms
موہوم (mawhum): Something uncertain or likely, but not certain; in this context, a potential cause of death that is not definitive.
ہوام (hawam): Insects or small creatures that crawl on the ground; their effect is unavoidable.
محرم (muharram): Prohibited; something that is forbidden to consume.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is a hunted animal haram if it has an additional wound from a source other than the hunter's arrow?
A) Because the hunter must not eat any animal that has been wounded by another person.
B) Because the additional wound is a case of mawhum (uncertainty) from which avoidance is possible, so it is treated like a certain cause of death.
C) Because the animal is considered carrion (maytah) if any other wound exists.
D) Because the hunter's arrow might have missed the vital area.

Key Takeaway
In hunting, an additional wound on the game that could have been avoided renders the meat haram, except for unavoidable sources such as insects.

Ruling on Mutaraddiyah: The Prohibition of Uncertain Kill
Ruling on hunted animal that falls after being shot

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mutaraddiyah and explain the reasoning based on the hadith and principle of uncertainty.

Core Idea
Uncertain cause of death makes a hunted animal haram — fall or drowning casts doubt.

This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling on a hunted animal that falls into water or from a height before dying. The Quranic text and a hadith from the Prophet (ﷺ) establish the prohibition, and the reasoning hinges on the possibility that the fall, rather than the arrow, caused death. Understanding this principle is crucial for hunters and those dealing with game meat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is hunting an animal that subsequently falls into water or from a height. The Hanafi ruling is that such an animal (muttaraddiyah) is haram (prohibited) to eat.
2
Examine the Quranic nass
The Quran explicitly mentions mutaraddiyah as prohibited in Surah al-Ma'idah (5:3). This is the primary textual basis for the ruling.
The term nass refers to clear textual evidence.
3
Analyze the supporting hadith
The hadith of 'Adi ibn Hatim (ﷺ) states: 'If your shot falls into water, do not eat, for you do not know whether the water killed it or your arrow.' This establishes the principle of avoiding when the cause of death is uncertain.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain) but accepted as proof.
4
Apply the principle of combining causes
When two possible causes (arrow and fall/water) coexist, the Hanafi school gives preference to the cause of prohibition (uncertainty). Thus, the animal is haram.
This is based on caution in matters of prohibition (ihtiyat).
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools may allow the animal if the arrow wound is clearly fatal. The Hanafis prioritize the uncertainty and maintain the prohibition.

Source Text

متردد یہ حرام ہے قال واذا رمى صيدا فوقع فى الماء او وقع على سطح او جبل ثم تردى منه الى الارض لم يوكل لانه المتردية وهو حرام بالنص ولانه احتمل الموت بغیر الرمی اذ الماء مهلک وكذا السقوط من عل يؤيد ذلك قوله عليه السلام لعدى رضی الله عنه وان وقعت رميتک فی الماء فلا تاكل فانک لا تدرى ان الماء قتله او سهمك ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جب اس نے شکار کو تیر مارا پس وہ شکار پانی میں گر گیا یا کسی چھت پر گرایا پہاڑ پر پھرلڑھک کر زمین پر گرا تو وہ نہیں کھایا جائے گا اس لئے کہ وہ متردیہ ہے اور وہ نص ( قرآنی) سے حرام ہے اور اس لئے کہ وہ احتمال رکھتا ہے موت کا بغیر تیر کے اس لئے کہ پانی ہلاک کرنے والا ہے اور ایسے بلندی سے گرنا عدگی سے نبی علیہ السلام کا فرمان اسکا مؤید ہے اگر تیر مارا ہوا شکار پانی میں گر جائے تو مت کھا اس لئے کہ تو نہیں جانتا کہ پانی نے اس کو مارا ہے یا تیرے تیر نے۔ تشریح متردید، جس کا بیان ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے نص قرآنی سے اس کی حرمت ثابت ہے لہذا اگر کسی شکار کو تیر مارا اور وہ زخمی ہو کر پانی میں گر گیا یا کسی چھت پر یا پہاڑ پر گر پھر وہاں سے لڑھکتا ہواز مین پر آیا اور وہ مرا ہوا ہے تو یہ متر دیہ ہے جو حرام ہے۔ نیز اس میں احتمال ہے کہ وہ تیر سے مرا ہو اور احتمال ہے کہ پانی کی وجہ سے مرا ہو یا اوپر سے لڑھکنے کی وجہ سے مرا ہو تو جب دوسبب جمع ہو گئے تو حسب اصول مذکور حرمت کے سبب کو ترجیح ہوتی ہے۔ نیز حضرت عدی ابن حاتم طائی سے جو آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا تھا اس میں بھی یہی حکم مذکور ہے حضرت نے فرمایا کہ جب تیرا تیر مارا ہوا شکار پانی میں گر جائے تو اس کو مت کھاؤ اس لئے کہ یہاں یہ معلوم نہیں کہ اس کی موت پانی میں گرنے سے واقع ہوتی ہے یا تیرے تیر کی وجہ سے۔
"Mutaraddi is haram." He (al-Quduri) said: And if he shot a hunted animal and it fell into water, or fell on a roof or a mountain, then rolled from there to the ground, it will not be eaten because it is mutaraddiyah (the animal that falls from a height), and it is haram by the text (of the Quran), and because it is possible that it died without the shooting, since water is a cause of destruction, and similarly falling from a height. This is supported by the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) to 'Adi (may Allah be pleased with him): "If your shot falls into water, do not eat, for you do not know whether the water killed it or your arrow." Translation: Al-Quduri said: And when he shot a hunted animal, then that hunted animal fell into water, or fell on a roof or mountain, then rolled and fell to the ground, it will not be eaten because it is mutaraddiyah, and it is haram by the text (of the Quran), and because it bears the possibility of death without the shooting, since water is destructive and similarly falling from a height. The saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) to 'Adi (may Allah be pleased with him) supports it: "If your shot falls into water, do not eat, for you do not know whether the water killed it or your arrow." Commentary: Mutaraddi, whose description has passed earlier, its prohibition is established by the Quranic text. Therefore, if someone shot a hunted animal and it, wounded, fell into water, or fell on a roof or mountain, then rolled from there onto the ground, and it is found dead, then this is mutaraddi, which is haram. Also, there is a possibility that it died from the arrow, and a possibility that it died from the water or from rolling from the height. So when two causes combine, according to the mentioned principle, the cause of prohibition is given preference. Also, from Hadrat 'Adi ibn Hatim al-Ta'i, the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed this: "When your shot falls into water, do not eat it, because it is not known whether its death occurred from falling into water or from your arrow."
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on a hunted animal that falls into water or from a height (muttaraddiyah). The author begins with the heading 'Mutaraddiyah is haram', then presents the original matn from al-Quduri: if a shot animal falls into water or falls on a roof/mountain and then rolls to the ground, it is not to be eaten. The proof is twofold: first, the Quranic text prohibiting mutaraddiyah (the animal that falls from a height); second, the possibility that death occurred from the fall or drowning rather than the arrow. This is further supported by the hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) to 'Adi ibn Hatim: if the shot falls into water, do not eat because you do not know which caused death. The commentary explains that when two causes combine (the arrow and the fall/water), the principle is to prefer the cause of prohibition (the fall/water) because it introduces uncertainty. Therefore, the animal is haram.

Key Terms
متردیہ (muttaraddiyah): An animal that falls from a height (like a cliff, roof, etc.) and dies; its meat is prohibited by Quranic text.
نص (nass): Here it refers to the clear text of the Quran (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:3) that prohibits mutaraddiyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is mutaraddiyah (an animal that falls from a height after being shot) haram in Hanafi fiqh?
A) Because the Quran explicitly prohibits it.
B) Because the animal is not properly slaughtered.
C) Because the cause of death is uncertain.
D) Because the animal fell from a height.

Key Takeaway
A hunted animal that falls into water or from a height after being shot is haram due to uncertainty in the cause of death.

Unavoidable Fall: Halal Hunt
Ruling when a hunted animal falls directly to the ground after being shot

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of ihtiraz to determine when a hunted animal is halal despite falling to the ground.

Core Idea
If the animal's fall is unavoidable, the uncertainty is ignored and the animal remains halal.

Hunting rules in the Hanafi school carefully consider whether the hunter could have avoided the animal's landing. The passage clarifies that when a hunted animal falls directly to the ground after being shot, it is halal because such a fall is unavoidable. If the fall were considered a cause of prohibition, no hunted animal could ever be eaten, closing the door of hunting entirely. This ruling contrasts with other scenarios (e.g., falling into water or from a height) where avoidance is possible and the animal is haram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is hunting with an arrow; the ruling is the permissibility (halal) of eating the animal when it falls directly to the ground.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
Contrast the direct fall to ground (halal) with an avoidable fall (e.g., into water, from a height) which is haram.
3
Locate the operative cause (illa)
The key factor is whether avoidance (ihtiraz) is possible. For direct ground fall, ihtiraz is impossible, so uncertainty is disregarded.
4
Apply the Hanafi principle
If avoidance is impossible, the cause of prohibition is ignored to keep the door of hunting open. This is a specific application of the broader usul principle that impossibility excuses.
5
Note cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Other schools may require certainty that the arrow caused death, but Hanafis accept direct fall as sufficient evidence due to unavoidability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان وقع على الارض ابتداء اكل لانه لا يمكن الاحتراز عنه وفى اعتباره سد باب الاصطياد بخلاف ما تقدم لانه يمكن التحرز عنه ترجمہ اور اگر شکار شروع ہی میں زمین پر گرا تو کھایا جائے گا اس لئے کہ اس سے احتراز ممکن نہیں ہے اور احتراز کے اعتبار کرنے میں شکار کے دروازہ کو بند کرنا ہے بخلاف پہلی صورت کے اس لئے کہ اس سے احتراز ممکن ہے۔ تشریح اگر شکار کو تیر لگ کر براہ راست زمین پر گرا اور مرگیا تو وہ حلال ہے کیونکہ شکار زمین کے اوپر تو ضرور ہی گرے گا اس کے علاوہ کوئی چارہ نہیں ہے اور پہاڑ وغیرہ پر گرنا کچھ لازم ضروری نہیں ہے بالفاظ دیگر زمین پر گرنے سے انتر از ممکن نہیں تو اس کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا اور شکار کو حلال کہا گیا ور نہ شکار کرنے کا دروازہ بند ہو جائے گا اور پہاڑ وغیرہ پر گرنا ایسی چیز ہے جس سے احتراز ممکن ہے اس وجہ سے اس کو حرام قرار دیا گیا ہے۔
"And if it falls on the ground initially, it is eaten, because avoidance from it is not possible, and in considering it there would be closing the door of hunting, unlike what preceded because avoidance from that is possible." Translation: And if the hunted animal initially falls on the ground, it will be eaten, because avoidance from it is not possible, and considering it (as a cause of prohibition) would close the door of hunting, unlike the previous case because avoidance from that is possible. Commentary: If the hunted animal is hit by an arrow and directly falls on the ground and dies, then it is halal, because the hunted animal must fall on the ground; there is no alternative. Falling on a mountain etc. is not necessary. In other words, falling on the ground cannot be avoided, so it is not considered (a cause of prohibition), and the hunted animal is declared halal. Otherwise, the door of hunting would be closed. Falling on a mountain etc. is something that can be avoided, therefore it has been declared haram.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage clarifies the ruling when a hunted animal falls directly on the ground after being shot, as opposed to falling into water or from a height. The author states that in this case the animal is halal because the hunter cannot avoid the animal falling to the ground—it is inevitable. If such a fall were considered a cause of prohibition, it would effectively close the door of hunting altogether, since every shot animal must eventually fall. In contrast, falling into water or from a height is avoidable, so those cases remain haram. The ruling is based on the principle that where avoidance is impossible, the uncertain cause is disregarded.

Key Terms
احتراز (ihteraz): Avoidance; in this context, the ability to prevent or avoid a potential cause of prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because the hunter cannot avoid the animal falling to the ground, so that uncertainty is disregarded.
C) Because the arrow always kills instantly when the animal hits the ground.
D) Because the animal is considered naturally dead by the strike.

Key Takeaway
A hunted animal that falls directly to the ground after being shot is halal because the fall is unavoidable; considering it would make hunting impossible.

The General Principle for Conflicting Causes of Halal and Haram
General principle for conflicting causes of halal and haram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle for conflicting causes of halal and haram, distinguishing when avoidance from the cause of haram is possible versus impossible.

Core Idea
When halal and haram causes combine, haram prevails if avoidable; if unavoidable, haram is disregarded.

This lesson presents a foundational principle in Hanafi fiqh: when causes of permissibility and prohibition converge, the school prioritizes prohibition as a precaution, but only if avoidance from the prohibited cause is possible. If avoidance is impossible, the prohibited cause is considered non-existent, and permissibility remains. This principle is rooted in the Quranic maxim that Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity (Surah al-Baqarah 2:286). Understanding this principle is essential for correctly applying rulings in hunting and other cases where multiple legal causes interact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Recognize a situation where both a cause making the thing halal (e.g., valid hunting intention) and a cause making it haram (e.g., death from an unavoidable fall) are present.
2
Locate the Cause of Haram
Determine the specific act or event that would normally render the animal haram. In hunting, common haram causes include death from a fall onto a sharp object or drowning.
3
Assess Avoidability
Ask: Was it possible for the hunter to avoid this haram cause? For example, could the hunter have prevented the animal from falling onto a sharp rock? If the fall was a direct result of the arrow and unavoidable, avoidance is impossible.
Avoidability is judged by normal human capacity, not by speculation.
4
Apply the Principle
If avoidance is possible, give preference to the haram cause (declare the meat haram). If avoidance is impossible, treat the haram cause as non-existent, leaving only the halal cause (meat is halal).
This balances precaution with the principle that obligation is according to capacity.
5
Confirm with the Quranic Maxim
Recall the verse 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.' This supports disregarding the haram cause when avoidance is impossible, as requiring avoidance would be a burden beyond human capacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصار الاصل ان سبب الحرمة والحل اذا اجتمعا وامكن التحرز عما هو سبب الحرمة ترجح احتياطاًوان كان ممالا يمكن التحرز عنه جرى وجوده مجرى عدمه لان التكليف بحسب الوسع ترجمہ تو قاعدہ کلیہ یہ ہو گیا کہ حرمت وحلت کا سبب جب دونوں جمع ہو جائیں اور حرمت کے سبب سے احتراز ممکن ہو تو بر بناء احتیاط حرمت کی جہت کو ترجیح دی جائے گی اور اگر وہ سبب ان چیزوں میں سے ہو جس سے بچاؤ ممکن نہیں ہے تو اس سبب کا وجوہ عارم سبب کے درجہ میں ہو گا اس لئے کہ تکلیف وسعت کے بقدر ہوتی ہے۔ تشریح مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ ہماری سابق تقریر سے ایک قاعدہ کلیہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ جب کسی چیز کی حلت و حرمت دونوں کے سبب جمع ہو جائیں تو اگر چہ حرمت کے سبب کو ترجیح دی جاتی ہے لیکن اس سے پہلے حرمت کے سبب پر غور کر لیا جائے کہ اس سے احتراز بھی ممکن ہے یا نہیں اگر احتر از ممکن ہو تو قاعدہ مذکورہ جاری کیا جائے گا یعنی حرمت کو ترجیح دی جائے گی اور اگر اس سے احتراز ممکن نہیں ہے جیسے شکار کا زمین پر گرنا تھا تو اس کو کالعدم شمار کیا جائے گا اور جب اس کو معدوم شمار کر لیا گیا تو اب فقط حلت کا سبب باقی رہ گیا لہذا شکار حلال ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اصول مقرر ہے کہ تکلیف بقدر وسعت ہوتی ہے فرمان باری ہے لا يكف الله نفساً الا وسعها وہ اسباب جن سے بچاؤ ممکن ہے اور جن سے بچاؤ ممکن نہیں فمما يمكن التحرز عنه موضع الى موضع حتى تردى الى الارض اورماه فوقع على رمح منصوب اوقصبة قائمة او على حرف آجرة لاحتمال ان حد هذه الاشياء قتله
"So the principle becomes: when the cause of prohibition and the cause of permission combine, and avoidance from the cause of prohibition is possible, the prohibition is given preference as a precaution. But if it is something from which avoidance is not possible, its existence is regarded as non-existence, because obligation is according to capacity." Translation: So a general rule has been established: when the causes of prohibition and permission both combine, and avoidance from the cause of prohibition is possible, then on the basis of precaution, the aspect of prohibition is given preference. And if that cause is among those from which avoidance is not possible, then the existence of that cause is in the level of non-existence, because obligation is according to capacity. Commentary: The author says that from our previous discussion, a general rule is known: when both causes of halal and haram combine for something, even though the cause of haram is given preference, but first it must be considered whether avoidance from the cause of haram is possible or not. If avoidance is possible, then the mentioned rule is applied, i.e., haram is given preference. And if avoidance from it is not possible, like the hunted animal's falling to the ground, then it is considered non-existent. And when it is considered non-existent, then only the cause of halal remains, so the hunted animal becomes halal. Because the established principle is that obligation is according to capacity. Allah says: 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:286). The causes from which avoidance is possible and those from which avoidance is not possible: among those from which avoidance is possible is when it falls from place to place until it rolls to the ground, or it falls on an erected spear, or a standing reed, or on the edge of a brick, due to the possibility that the sharpness of these things killed it...
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage presents a general principle (qaidah kulliyah) derived from the preceding rulings. When causes of halal and haram combine, the haram cause prevails if avoidance is possible. If avoidance is impossible (like falling directly to ground), the haram cause is disregarded and the animal is halal. The author cites the Quranic principle that obligation is according to capacity (la yukallifu Allahu nafsan illa wus'aha). Then he begins listing examples of avoidable causes: falling from place to place until rolling to the ground, falling on an erected spear, a standing reed, or the edge of a brick, because these sharp objects might have killed it. The text is cut off, but the rule is established.

Key Terms
قاعدہ کلیہ (qaidah kulliyah): A general legal principle that governs multiple related rulings; here it states how to prioritize when causes of halal and haram combine.
تکلیف بحسب الوسع (taklif bihasab al-wus'): Obligation is according to capacity; a Quranic principle meaning Allah does not require what is beyond one's ability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the general principle in Hanafi fiqh, when causes of halal and haram combine, what is the primary factor in determining which prevails?
A) The strength of the evidence for each cause.
B) Whether avoidance from the cause of haram is possible.
C) The intention of the hunter.
D) The type of animal hunted.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle for conflicting causes: haram overrides halal only if avoidance from haram is possible; otherwise, haram is considered non-existent.

Ruling on Game Falling Directly to Ground
States the ruling and proof for game falling directly to ground

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on game that falls directly to the ground and explain the rational proof (dalil aqli) that supports it.

Core Idea
If game falls directly to ground after being shot, it is halal because avoiding the fall is impossible.

In the Book of Hunting, a key question arises: when a hunter shoots an animal and it falls directly to the ground and dies, is it halal or haram? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on a rational principle: what is unavoidable is excused. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proof, contrasting it with a related case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the specific scenario described? The game is shot, falls directly to the ground, and dies. State the hukm (halal or haram) as given in the text.
The text explicitly says 'halal' / 'eaten'.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
What proof does the author cite? The proof is a rational argument (dalil aqli), not a text from Quran or Hadith. Find the key phrase in the Arabic: 'لانه لا يمكن الاحتراز عنه وفى اعتباره سد باب الاصطياد'.
The proof is based on the impossibility of avoiding the fall.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof proves the ruling)
Explain the logical link: The fall to ground is unavoidable. If we considered it a cause of prohibition (haram), then hunters would have to prevent the game from hitting the ground entirely, which is impossible. Therefore, the falling to ground is disregarded, and the game remains halal.
The key term is 'ihtiraz' (avoidance).
4
Note the contrast with the previous case
The text mentions 'unlike what preceded' – referring to a scenario where the game falls on a mountain or tree first. In that case, avoidance is possible (e.g., by aiming differently), so it becomes haram. Identify the distinguishing factor.
This contrast reinforces the principle of avoidability.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Is there any disagreement? The Hanafi position is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi). Some scholars might argue that if the impact with the ground kills it, it becomes carrion. However, the Hanafi school prioritizes the principle of necessity (darurah) and the prevention of hardship.
The concept of 'sadd al-bab' (closing the door) is invoked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شکار کو تیر لگا اور براہ راست زمین پر گرا اور مر گیا تو وہ شکار حلال ہے
وان وقع على الارض ابتداء اكل لانه لا يمكن الاحتراز عنه وفى اعتباره سد باب الاصطياد بخلاف ما تقدم لانه يمكن التحرز عنه
ترجمہ اور اگر شکار شروع ہی میں زمین پر گرا تو کھایا جائے گا اس لئے کہ اس سے احتراز ممکن نہیں ہے اور احتراز کے اعتبار کرنے میں شکار کے دروازہ کو بند کرنا ہے بخلاف پہلی صورت کے اس لئے کہ اس سے احتراز ممکن ہے۔
تشریح اگر شکار کو تیر لگ کر براہ راست زمین پر گرا اور مرگیا تو وہ حلال ہے کیونکہ شکار زمین کے اوپر تو ضرور ہی گرے گا اس کے علاوہ کوئی چارہ نہیں ہے اور پہاڑ وغیرہ پر گرنا کچھ لازم ضروری نہیں ہے بالفاظ دیگر زمین پر گرنے سے انتر از ممکن نہیں تو اس کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا اور شکار کو حلال کہا گیا ور نہ شکار کرنے کا دروازہ بند ہو جائے گا اور پہاڑ وغیرہ پر گرنا ایسی چیز ہے جس سے احتراز ممکن ہے اس وجہ سے اس کو حرام قرار دیا گیا ہے۔
When the game is hit by an arrow and falls directly to the ground and dies, that game is halal. And if it falls to the ground initially, it is eaten because it is not possible to avoid it, and considering avoidance would close the door of hunting, unlike what preceded because avoidance is possible. Translation: And if the game falls to the ground initially, it will be eaten because avoidance from it is not possible, and considering avoidance would close the door of hunting, unlike the previous case because avoidance is possible. Explanation: If the game is hit by an arrow and falls directly to the ground and dies, it is halal because the game must fall to the ground, there is no alternative, and falling on a mountain etc. is not necessary. In other words, avoidance from falling to the ground is not possible, so it is not considered, and the game is declared halal, otherwise the door of hunting would be closed. And falling on a mountain etc. is something avoidance from which is possible, therefore it is declared haram.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Book of Hunting. The author first states the ruling in Urdu: if the game is hit by an arrow and falls directly to the ground and dies, it is halal. Then the Arabic text from the Hidayah is quoted: 'And if it falls to the ground initially, it is eaten because it is not possible to avoid it, and considering avoidance would close the door of hunting, unlike what preceded because avoidance is possible.' The Urdu translation and explanation follow. The ruling is based on the principle that what is unavoidable is excused. Since the game must eventually fall to the ground, it is impossible to prevent that. If we were to require that the game not touch the ground at all, hunting would become impossible. Therefore, the cause of potential haram (like dying from the fall) is disregarded. This is contrasted with the previous case (mentioned earlier in the text) where the game falls on a mountain or tree first, because there avoidance is possible by aiming differently.

Key Terms
احتراز (ihtiraz): Avoidance or precaution; the ability to prevent or avoid a cause.
سبب الحرمة (sabab al-hurma): The cause of prohibition; here, the game's fall to the ground which could cause death by impact.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the game halal when it falls directly to the ground after being shot?
A) Because the arrow killed it
B) Because avoidance from falling to ground is impossible
C) Because the ground is pure
D) Because the hunter intended to shoot

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that game falling directly to ground is halal because avoidance is impossible, and requiring it would render hunting impractical.

The Maxim of Combining Causes of Halal and Haram
Establishes a general legal maxim and lists its applications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim for combining causes of halal and haram and apply it to hunting scenarios by distinguishing avoidable and unavoidable causes.

Core Idea
When the cause of haram is avoidable, it prevails; if unavoidable, it is disregarded — obligation is according to capacity.

This lesson presents a key legal maxim from the Hidayah's Book of Hunting. The maxim resolves conflicts when both halal and haram causes are present. The Hanafi school uses the principle of taklif bi hasab al-wus' to determine which cause overrides. Through concrete examples of game falling on different surfaces, you will learn how to apply this maxim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim's statement
Read the first part of the source to extract the maxim: when causes of halal and haram combine, and the cause of haram is avoidable, it is given precedence; if unavoidable, it is treated as non-existent.
The maxim is explicitly stated as 'al-asl anna sabab al-hurma wa al-hill idha ijtama'a...'
2
Understand the condition of avoidability
The key condition is ihtiraz (avoidance). Determine whether the cause of haram can be avoided. If yes, haram prevails; if no, the cause is ignored.
Avoidability is assessed based on normal circumstances, not rare accidents.
3
See the proof from Quran
The maxim is justified by the Quranic principle that obligation is according to capacity (2:286). Unavoidable matters are not considered in the cause of prohibition.
The proof is not directly about hunting but is applied analogically.
4
Apply to avoidable causes
Review the seven listed avoidable causes: falling on a tree, wall, baked brick, mountain with rolling, erected spear, standing bamboo, or brick edge. In each, the game is haram because the fall could have been avoided.
These are considered avoidable because they are not inevitable; the hunter could have prevented them.
5
Apply to unavoidable causes
Review the two unavoidable causes: falling directly on the ground, or on a mountain/roof/unbaked brick/rock (which are like ground). In these, the game is halal because the cause of haram cannot be avoided.
The reason is that such falls are indistinguishable from the natural death of the game.

ا۔ شکار کا زمین پر گرنا
-۲ پہاڑ پر گرنا
The general principle: When the causes of prohibition and permissibility combine, and avoidance of the cause of prohibition is possible, then the aspect of prohibition is given precedence as a precaution. If avoidance is not possible, then its existence is treated as non-existence because the obligation is according to capacity. Translation: So the general principle is that when the causes of prohibition and permissibility both combine, and avoidance from the cause of prohibition is possible, then based on precaution the aspect of prohibition is given precedence. And if that cause is among those things from which avoidance is not possible, then that cause's existence is treated as non-existence because obligation is according to capacity. Explanation: The author says that from our previous discussion a general principle is understood: when the causes of halal and haram combine, the cause of haram is given precedence, but first it is considered whether avoidance from it is possible. If avoidance is possible, the above rule is applied (haram prevails). If avoidance is not possible, like the game falling to ground, then it is considered non-existent, and only the cause of halal remains, so the game is halal. This is because the established principle is that obligation is according to capacity, as Allah says: 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.' (Quran 2:286). The causes from which avoidance is possible and those from which it is not: Among those from which avoidance is possible: when it falls on a tree, then wall, then baked brick, then falls to ground; or when the game is shot and it rolls from place to place until it reaches the ground; or when it falls on an erected spear, or on a standing bamboo, or on the edge of a brick, due to the possibility that the edge of these things killed it. Translation: So among the causes from which avoidance is possible: when the game falls on a tree, or on a wall, or on a baked brick, then falls to ground; or the game is shot and it is on a mountain, then it rolls from one place to another until it reaches the ground; or when it is shot and it falls on an erected spear, or on a standing bamboo, or on the edge of a baked brick, due to the possibility that the edge of these things killed it. Explanation: When the author stated the general principle, it became necessary to clarify which causes avoidance is possible and which not. So the author detailed them. Avoidable causes are: 1. Falling on a tree after being hit, 2. Falling on a wall, 3. Falling on a baked brick, 4. Falling on a mountain and then rolling to ground, 5. Falling on an erected spear, 6. Falling on a standing bamboo, 7. Falling on the edge of a baked brick and dying. In these, there is a possibility that the edge of these things killed it, so there is a second possibility, and since avoidance is possible, the aforementioned rule is applied: the aspect of prohibition is given precedence and the game is haram. These are considered avoidable because the game does not always do this; it happens due to circumstances, so it is called possible to avoid. Unavoidable causes: And among those from which avoidance is not possible: when it falls on the ground as we mentioned, or on what is in its meaning like a mountain, or the roof of a house, or a laid unbaked brick, or a rock, and it settles there, because its falling on these and on the ground is the same. Explanation: From here the description of causes from which avoidance is not possible is given; they are considered non-existent and the game is declared halal. They are: 1. The game falling on the ground, 2. Falling on a mountain.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage presents a general legal maxim from the Book of Hunting of the Hidayah. The ruling is that when causes of halal and haram combine, the cause of haram is given precedence if it is avoidable; if unavoidable, it is disregarded. The proof is the Quranic principle that obligation is according to capacity. The text then lists seven avoidable causes: falling on a tree, wall, baked brick, mountain with rolling, erected spear, standing bamboo, or brick edge. In these cases, because there is a possibility that the sharp edge caused death, and because such falls are not inevitable, the game is considered haram. Then two unavoidable causes are listed: falling directly on the ground, or on a mountain, roof, unbaked brick, or rock (which are like ground). In these, since avoidance is impossible, the cause of haram is disregarded, and the game is halal. This maxim applies throughout Hanafi fiqh wherever causes combine.

Key Terms
قاعدہ کلیہ (qa'ida kulliyya): A general legal maxim derived from specific rulings.
سبب الحرمة (sabab al-hurma): The cause that leads to the game being prohibited, such as dying from an avoidable fall.
احتراز (ihtiraz): Avoidance; the ability to prevent the cause of haram from occurring.
تكليف بحسب الوسع (taklif bi hasab al-wus'): Legal obligation is according to one's capacity; a foundational principle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi maxim, what is the ruling if a hunted animal dies from falling on an avoidable surface like the edge of a baked brick?
A) Halal, because the ground is unavoidable.
B) Haram, because the avoidable cause of haram prevails.
C) Halal, because the hunter did not intend the fall.
D) Haram only if the brick is unbaked.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim resolves conflicts of halal and haram causes by giving precedence to the avoidable cause of haram; unavoidable causes are disregarded due to the principle of obligation according to capacity.

Avoidable vs Unavoidable Secondary Causes in Hunting
Author enumerates avoidable and unavoidable causes in hunting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the lawfulness of hunted meat based on whether the secondary cause of death was avoidable, and distinguish between avoidable and unavoidable causes using the examples provided.

Core Idea
In hunting, meat is lawful if the secondary cause is unavoidable, but unlawful if the hunter could have avoided the hazard.

The Hanafi school establishes a key principle: if a hunted animal dies from a secondary cause that the hunter could have prevented, the meat is haram. The author expands on this by categorising specific scenarios into avoidable (mumkin al-ihtiraz) and unavoidable (ma'dum al-ihtiraz), with clear examples for each.

Guided Path
1
Understand the general rule
The meat is halal only if the secondary cause of death (e.g., the surface the animal falls on) is unavoidable. If the hunter could have taken precautions to prevent the animal from hitting a hazardous object, the meat is haram.
This rule is stated earlier in the text; here the author provides concrete examples.
2
Identify avoidable causes
From the text, list the scenarios where the hunter could have avoided the secondary cause: planted spear, standing bamboo, edge of baked brick, etc. Note why each is avoidable—they are not inevitable outcomes.
These are cases where the animal does not always fall on such objects; they are exceptional.
3
Identify unavoidable causes
List the scenarios where avoidance is impossible: falling on the ground, mountain, rooftop, unbaked brick, or rock. These are considered equivalent to the ground because the animal inevitably lands on something.
The key is that these surfaces are a normal part of the environment and cannot be avoided.
4
Apply the distinction
Given a new scenario, determine whether the secondary cause is avoidable or unavoidable. If avoidable, the meat is haram; if unavoidable, it is halal.
The possibility of avoidance is assessed from the hunter's perspective—could he have taken preventive measures?

۴۔ پڑی ہوئی کچی اینٹ پر گرنا
-۵- کسی بڑے پتھر پر گرنا ، اور جہاں گر گیا ہے وہیں ٹھہرا رہنا اور مر جانا ورنہ اگر پہاڑ پر گر کر زمین پر لڑھک کر آیا ہے تو وہ حرام ہے ( کمامر ) تو ان سب صورتوں میں مراد یہ ہے کہ وہ ان کے اوپر گر کر وہیں ٹھہر جائے تو اب شکار کا ان چیزوں پر گرنا اور زمین پر گرنا برابر ہے۔

شکار پتھر پر گر گیا اور ٹھہر گیا تو حلال ہے
Book of Hunting. He fell on a planted spear, or on a standing bamboo, or on the edge of a baked brick, due to the possibility that the edge of these things killed him. Explanation: When the author stated the general rule, then it was necessary to clarify which are the causes from which avoidance is possible and which are the causes from which avoidance is not possible. So here the author has detailed those causes. First he mentions those from which avoidance is possible, then those from which avoidance is not possible. Those from which avoidance is possible are: 1. Falling on a tree after being hit by an arrow, 2. Falling on a wall, 3. Falling on a baked brick, 4. Falling on a mountain and then rolling down to the ground, 5. Falling on a planted spear, 6. Falling on a standing bamboo or spear, 7. Falling on the edge of a baked brick and dying. Due to the possibility that the edge of these things killed him, and since another possibility arises and avoidance is possible, the principle gives precedence to prohibition and the hunting is unlawful. Avoidance from all these mentioned causes is possible because the hunted animal does not always do this; rather it happens occasionally due to circumstances, therefore it is called possible to avoid. Those causes from which avoidance is not possible: And among those from which avoidance is not possible: when it falls on the ground as we mentioned, or on something equivalent to it, like a mountain, or a roof of a house, or an unbaked brick, or a rock, and it settles there, because its falling on them and on the ground is the same. Translation: And among those causes from which avoidance is not possible, when the hunted animal falls on the ground as we have mentioned, or on something that is in the status of the ground, like a mountain, or a roof of a house, or a lying unbaked brick, or a rock, then it settles there, because the animal's falling on these and on the ground is equal. Explanation: From here is the description of those causes from which avoidance is not possible, which are considered non-existent, and the hunted animal is declared lawful. They are: 1. The animal falling on the ground, 2. Falling on a mountain, 3. Falling on a roof of a house, 4. Falling on a lying unbaked brick, 5. Falling on a large rock, and it remains where it fell and dies. Otherwise, if it fell on a mountain and rolled to the ground, then it is unlawful (as before). In all these forms, the meaning is that it falls on them and settles there, so the animal's falling on these and falling on the ground is equal. If the animal fell on a rock and settled, it is lawful.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the general rule previously stated by the author. The author first lists scenarios where the hunter could have avoided the secondary cause of death—such as the animal falling on a planted spear, standing bamboo, or the edge of a baked brick. In these cases, since there is a possibility that the sharp edge caused the death, and the hunter could have avoided that possibility by taking preventive measures, the meat is unlawful. The criterion is whether the secondary cause is typical or exceptional; if it is exceptional and avoidable, the meat is haram. Then the author lists scenarios where avoidance is impossible: falling directly on the ground, or on something equivalent to the ground like a mountain, rooftop, unbaked brick, or a rock. In these cases, the animal would have died anyway from the fall itself, and the secondary cause (the surface) is unavoidable because it is the natural outcome of the fall. Therefore, the meat is lawful. The commentary emphasizes that the key distinction is whether the secondary cause is a normal consequence of the fall (like hitting the ground) or an abnormal, avoidable hazard (like a sharp object).

Key Terms
احتراز (ihtiraz): Avoidance of the secondary cause of death in hunting, i.e., the hunter's ability to prevent the animal from hitting a hazardous object.
ممكن الاحتراز (mumkin al-ihtiraz): A secondary cause that can be avoided by the hunter, e.g., a planted spear or standing bamboo, because the animal does not always fall on them.
معدوم الاحتراز (ma'dum al-ihtiraz): A secondary cause that cannot be avoided, e.g., falling on the ground or a rock, because the animal always lands on such surfaces.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a hunter's arrow hits a deer, and the deer falls onto a planted spear and dies, what is the ruling on eating its meat?
A) Halal, because the arrow caused the death.
B) Halal, because the spear is like the ground.
C) Haram, because the hunter could have avoided the spear.
D) Haram, because the deer died from the spear, not the arrow.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, hunted meat is lawful only if the secondary cause of death was unavoidable; if the hunter could have prevented the animal from hitting a hazardous object, the meat is unlawful.

Animal Falling on Rock: Reconciling Al-Mabsut and Al-Muntaka
Imam Sarakhsi reconciles al-Muntaka and al-Mabsut narrations on rock-split belly

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a hunted animal that falls on a rock and its belly splits, and explain Imam al-Sarakhsi's reconciliation of the two narrations.

Core Idea
A split belly from a rock's edge is haram; a split from blunt impact is halal — the cause of death determines the ruling.

This is an intra-Hanafi dispute where two authoritative texts seem to contradict each other. Imam al-Sarakhsi resolves the apparent contradiction by carefully examining the cause of death. The lesson trains you to apply legal reasoning (ta'lil) to reconcile prima facie conflicting rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two narrations
Imam Muhammad in al-Mabsut says the meat is halal unconditionally. Al-Hakim al-Shahid in al-Muntaka says if the belly splits, it is haram due to possibility of another cause.
2
Understand al-Hakim al-Shahid's interpretation
He interprets Imam Muhammad's absolute statement as limited to cases where the belly does not split. He relies on the principle of avoiding uncertainty (shubha).
3
Analyze Imam al-Sarakhsi's reconciliation
Sarakhsi distinguishes between two scenarios: if the rock's sharp edge causes a gash, the animal died from an additional cause (haram); if the belly splits from blunt impact similar to falling on ground, it is excused (halal).
This is based on the underlying cause (illa) of death.
4
Apply the reconciled ruling
When a hunter sees the animal fall and its belly split, he must determine whether a sharp edge caused a gash (haram) or it was a blunt impact (halal).
If uncertain, the default is permissibility (istishab).

Source Text

ترجمہ اور منتقی میں مذکور ہے کہ اگر شکار پتھر پرگرا پس اس کا پیٹ پھٹ گیا تو نہیں کھایا جائے گا دوسرے سبب سے موت کے احتمال کی وجہ سے اور اسی کو حاکم شہید نے صحیح قرار دیا ہے اور حاکم شہید نے مبسوط کی مطلق روایت کو پیٹ نہ پھٹنے کی حالت پر محمول کیا ہے اور شمس الائمہ سرخسی نے قول حاکم شہید کو اس شکار پر محمول کیا ہے جس کو پتھر کی دھار لگ گئی ہو پس اس کی وجہ سے اس کا پیٹ پھٹ گیا ہو اور سرخسی نے محمول کیا ہے اس روایت کو جو مبسوط میں مروی ہے اس حالت پر کہ شکار کو پکی اینٹ سے چوٹ نہ پہنچی ہو مگر اتنی ہی کہ جو اس کو زمین سے پہنچتی ہے اگر وہ زمین پر گرتا اور یہ معاف ہے اور یہ اصح ہے۔

تشریح منتقی حاکم شہید کی کتاب ہے مبسوط امام محمد کی تصنیف ہے امام سرخسی نے مبسوط کی شرح لکھی ہے جو بہت منعیم ہے۔ امام محمد نے مبسوط میں فرمایا ہے کہ اگر شکار پتھر گر گیا اور ٹھہر گیا تو حلال ہے یعنی خواہ اس کا پیٹ پھٹا ہو یا نہ پھٹا ہو اس بارے میں ان کا قول مطلق ہے اور حاکم شہید نے اپنی کتاب منتقی میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ اگر شکار پتھر پرگر اور اس کا پیٹ پھٹ گیا تو حرام ہے کھایا نہیں جائے گا کیونکہ رمی کے علاوہ دوسرے سبب سے مرنے کا احتمال ہے اور اس کو ذکر کر کے حاکم شہید نے اس کو صحیح قرار دیا ہے اور حاکم شہید نے کہا ہے کہ مبسوط کا جزئیہ کہ حلال ہے اس کا عمل یہ ہے کہ اس کا پیٹ نہ پھٹا ہو ورنہ حرام ہوگا۔
